**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**TO:** Congressional Leadership, Democratic & Republican
**FROM:** Chief News Analyst
**DATE:** July 19, 2025
**SUBJECT:** Daily Intelligence Briefing

**OVERVIEW**

Three overlapping crises dominate today's intelligence landscape. **First,** the Epstein investigation is accelerating into a constitutional clash, pitting the Executive Branch against both Congress and the Judiciary. The central flashpoint is now President Trump's direct, personal connection to the sealed files, following confirmation that Attorney General Pam Bondi briefed him on their contents. **Second,** the Administration is leveraging a significant Supreme Court victory to systemically reshape the federal government, moving to assert greater control over independent agencies while simultaneously preparing to dismantle the EPA’s legal authority to regulate climate change. **Third,** the 2026 midterm battleground is being defined, with Democrats launching a major challenge in the North Carolina Senate race and both parties mobilizing financial resources for early, high-stakes fights over redistricting.

---
### **Area 1: The Epstein Investigation**

**Topic 1.1: President Trump's Alleged Connection to Files**

The controversy surrounding the Jeffrey Epstein files has intensified significantly, with multiple high-credibility reports alleging the President’s personal involvement. The New York Times reported that Attorney General Pam Bondi personally informed President Trump that his name appeared in the Epstein files [1, 2]. This briefing, which reportedly took place in the spring, also included the information that many other individuals were named in the files [3]. Crucially, this conversation reportedly occurred before the Department of Justice made the decision to withhold the documents from public release, a timeline underscored by stories from both CNBC and People magazine based on the Wall Street Journal's initial reporting [4, 5].

The White House’s public response has been inconsistent. It initially issued a statement to Reuters calling the Wall Street Journal's story "fake" [6]. However, a subsequent report from the same outlet, citing an unnamed official, clarified that the White House is not denying that the President’s name appears in the files, creating public and political confusion [7]. This narrative is amplified by the separate emergence of photographs showing Jeffrey Epstein attending President Trump's 1993 wedding at Mar-a-Lago [8].

**References:**
[1] Attorney General Told Trump His Name Appeared in Epstein Files, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/23/us/politics/trump-epstein-files-named.html?smid=tw-nytimes&smtyp=cur

[2] Bondi briefed Trump that his name was in Epstein files, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/23/politics/bondi-trump-epstein-list-files

[3] Pam Bondi reportedly told Donald Trump in May that he's named in Epstein files | The attorney general reportedly told President Donald Trump in the spring that he and many others were named in the government's files on Jeffrey Epstein., https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/07/23/donald-trump-jeffrey-epstein-files-pam-bondi-meeting/85347573007/

[4] Trump was told his name was in Jeffrey Epstein files before DOJ withheld documents: WSJ, https://www.cnbc.com/amp/2025/07/23/trump-jeffrey-epstein-files-wsj.html

[5] DOJ Told Trump That He Appeared in Epstein Files Multiple Times Before Choosing to Halt Their Release: Report, https://people.com/doj-trump-appeared-epstein-files-multiple-times-before-halt-release-report-11777834?utm_campaign=peoplemagazine&utm_medium=social&utm_source=reddit.com&utm_content=post

[8] Photos emerge of Epstein at Trump’s wedding in 1993, https://www.channel4.com/news/photos-emerge-of-epstein-at-trumps-wedding-in-1993

**Topic 1.2: Congressional Investigations and Subpoenas**

Congressional inquiries are proceeding with bipartisan urgency. A Republican-led House Oversight subcommittee has officially voted to subpoena the Department of Justice, demanding access to its complete files on Jeffrey Epstein [1, 2]. This move represents a direct challenge to the administration’s control over the sensitive documents. In parallel, Oversight Chairman James Comer has issued a separate subpoena to compel a deposition from Epstein associate Ghislaine Maxwell at the federal prison where she is currently incarcerated [3, 4].

In the Senate, Finance Committee Ranking Member Ron Wyden has publicly detailed a "'Follow the Money' Investigation" plan. Citing what his office calls a "Trump’s Idle Department of Justice," Wyden outlined seven major lines of financial inquiry, putting further pressure on the administration to act on long-dormant aspects of the case [5].

**References:**
[1] Republican-led House panel votes to subpoena Jeffrey Epstein files, https://www.axios.com/2025/07/23/jeffrey-epstein-subpoena-republicans-democrats

[2] House Oversight subcommittee votes to subpoena the Department of Justice for Epstein files, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/23/politics/house-epstein-files-subpoena

[3] House committee subpoenas Epstein associate Ghislaine Maxwell to sit for deposition, https://apnews.com/article/epstein-files-congress-democrats-subpoena-republicans-trump-5d17ea83f7ffeff5784159848b97f38e

Years into His Own Epstein Investigation, Finance Ranking Democrat Recommends Seven Major Lines of Investigation for Trump’s Idle Department of Justice, https://www.finance.senate.gov/ranking-members-news/as-trump-sits-on-key-epstein-files-wyden-lays-out-follow-the-money-investigation-for-doj

**Topic 1.3: Department of Justice and Court Actions**

The judicial branch has weighed in on the disclosure of records related to the original Epstein probe, limiting one potential avenue for information release. A federal judge has declined a request to unseal grand jury documents from the criminal investigation that took place in Florida [1]. This ruling, reported by both CNN and CNBC, specifically rejected a legal bid made by the Trump administration to release the transcripts [2]. This court decision effectively places even greater emphasis on the Department of Justice's own internal files, which are now the subject of the formal congressional subpoena.

**References:**
[1] Judge declines to release grand jury documents from the criminal probe into Jeffrey Epstein, https://edition.cnn.com/2025/07/23/politics/judge-declines-grand-jury-documents-jeffrey-epstein

[2] Judge denies Trump admin bid to unseal Jeffrey Epstein grand jury transcripts in Florida, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/23/epstein-trump-grand-jury-florida.html

**Topic 1.4: Political and Media Commentary**

The political fallout from the Epstein files is creating unusual alliances and stressing party cohesion. Polling data reported by The New York Times suggests a segment of the Republican base is "breaking with Trump over Epstein files," indicating potential erosion of support [1]. Meanwhile, Speaker of the House Mike Johnson has publicly questioned the integrity of the documents, suggesting to Latin Times that the files might have been "'doctored' by [the] Biden Administration," which he called "'crooked and corrupt'" [2]. In a notable political crossover, Representative Thomas Massie, often characterized as a "Trump foe," is reportedly gaining significant support from "MAGA allies" for his aggressive push to release the files [3]. In contrast to the intense focus from others, Democratic Senator John Fetterman has reportedly dismissed the controversy, though the details of his comments are not specified [4].

**References:**
[1] Republicans Are Breaking With Trump Over Epstein Files, Polls Show, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/23/us/politics/epstein-trump-republicans.html?unlocked_article_code=1.Yk8.ShHX.egvvKqqK19p5&smid=url-share

[2] Mike Johnson Hints Epstein Files Were 'Doctored' by Biden Administration: 'Crooked and Corrupt', https://www.latintimes.com/mike-johnson-hints-epstein-files-were-doctored-biden-administration-crooked-corrupt-587461

[3] Trump foe Thomas Massie wins over MAGA allies with his push for Epstein files, https://www.nbcnews.com/politics/congress/trump-foe-thomas-massie-wins-maga-allies-push-epstein-files-rcna220586

[4] Democratic Sen. Fetterman dismisses Epstein controversy, https://www.waaytv.com/video/democratic-sen-fetterman-dismisses-epstein-controversy/video_75070a65-cd4f-533e-83d1-b93ee7371ed2.html

### **Area 2: Executive Branch: Actions, Policy, and Personnel**

**Topic 2.1: Executive Power and the Judiciary**

The administration has secured a significant legal victory at the Supreme Court that materially expands presidential authority. In a ruling reported by the Associated Press and The New York Times, the Court affirmed that President Trump has the power to remove three sitting Democratic members from the Consumer Product Safety Commission [1, 2]. This decision is a major win for the administration, validating a more muscular interpretation of executive power over independent federal agencies and delivering on a long-standing goal of increasing presidential control over the regulatory state [3].

**References:**
[1] The Supreme Court allows Trump to remove three Democrats on the Consumer Product Safety Commission, https://apnews.com/article/supreme-court-trump-consumer-product-safety-f0ed5ff2409287440f5067d64031429d?utm_source=onesignal&utm_medium=push&utm_campaign=2025-07-23-Breaking+News

[2] Supreme Court Lets Trump Fire Consumer Product Safety Regulators, https://www.nytimes.com/2025/07/23/us/politics/supreme-court-consumer-product-commission.html?smid=url-share

[3] Supreme Court hands Trump a win on Consumer Product Safety Commission firings, https://www.usatoday.com/story/news/politics/2025/07/23/supreme-court-trump-consumer-product-safety-commission/85196601007/

**Topic 2.2: Personnel: Conduct, Nominations, and Investigations**

Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth is now under a formal investigation by the Pentagon's Inspector General for his handling of sensitive information. According to sources cited by CNN and CBS News, the watchdog has obtained evidence that Secretary Hegseth's messages on the encrypted Signal app, including some concerning military strikes in Yemen, "included info from classified email" [1, 2]. This raises serious national security and protocol questions. Separately, a key diplomatic appointment is stalled in the Senate. According to Axios, Senator Rand Paul is single-handedly holding up the nomination of Mike Waltz to serve as the U.S. Ambassador to the United Nations [3].

**References:**
[1] Pentagon watchdog has evidence Hegseth’s Signal messages included classified information, sources say, https://www.cnn.com/2025/07/23/politics/pentagon-watchdog-evidence-hegseth-signal-messages

[2] Hegseth's Signal messages on Yemen strikes included info from classified email, watchdog learns, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/hegseth-signal-messages-yemen-strikes-classified-email-trump-administration/

[3] Scoop: Rand Paul stalls Mike Waltz nomination for UN ambassador, https://www.axios.com/2025/07/23/rand-paul-mike-waltz-nomination-un-ambassador

**Topic 2.3: Environmental and Public Health Regulations**

The administration is preparing a foundational challenge to federal environmental law. According to sources speaking to CNN, the White House will soon "propose to kill EPA’s ability to make rules about climate pollution" [1]. This would be accomplished by repealing the agency's official endangerment finding—the legal conclusion that greenhouse gases threaten public health and welfare. As reported by The Hill, this action would dismantle the legal underpinning for a wide range of current and future emissions regulations [2]. In a separate and controversial public health matter, a report from The Daily Beast alleges the administration "plans to burn $10 Million Worth of Contraceptives for Poor Nations" [3]. No additional details on this plan were available in the news feed.

**References:**
[1] Trump admin will soon propose to kill EPA’s ability to make rules about climate pollution, sources say, https://edition.cnn.com/2025/07/23/climate/epa-greenhouse-gas-endangerment

[2] Trump EPA will propose repealing finding that climate change endangers public health, http://thehill.com/policy/energy-environment/5416694-epa-proposes-repeal-2009-determination/

[3] Trump Admin Plans to Burn $10 Million Worth of Contraceptives for Poor Nations, https://www.thedailybeast.com/trump-admin-plans-to-burn-10-million-worth-of-contraceptives-for-poor-nations/

**Topic 2.4: Immigration and Border Policy**

The administration's efforts to expand immigration enforcement and detention capacity are moving forward. According to the New York Post, the administration is set to open the nation's largest immigration detention center in Texas, a project established via a massive $1.2 billion contract [1]. On the enforcement front, a CBS News analysis of government data shows that Immigration and Customs Enforcement (ICE) is on pace to conduct the most deportations since the Obama administration. However, the report also notes that this pace remains "far short" of the President’s publicly stated target of deporting one million people annually [2].

**References:**
[1] Trump admin to open nation’s largest immigration detention center in Texas with $1.2B contract, https://nypost.com/2025/07/23/us-news/trump-admin-to-open-nations-largest-immigration-detention-center-in-texas-with-1-2b-contract/?utm_medium=social&utm_source=twitter&utm_campaign=nypost

[2] ICE on track for most deportations since Obama years, but still far short of 1 million target, https://www.cbsnews.com/news/ice-deportations-trump-six-months/

**Topic 2.5: Economic, Trade, and Technology Policy**

In a recent policy speech on artificial intelligence reported by Wired, President Trump declared he is "'getting rid of woke'" in the technology sector and broadly dismissed concerns related to copyright protections for creators [1]. On international trade, the Justice Department is reportedly preparing a new "crackdown on Trump tariff violators," signaling a new phase of enforcement for the administration's signature economic policy [2]. Regarding former tech czar Elon Musk, the White House has publicly stated that it does not want Musk's company, xAI, to be awarded any government contracts [3]. In a separate business development, NBC News reports that Tesla, Musk's electric vehicle company, "continues its financial downturn even after Elon Musk's White House exit," [4].

**Topic 2.6: Other Administration Actions and Communications**

Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard has officially released a House Intelligence Report which, according to a Breitbart headline, purports to detail how the Obama administration “‘manufactured’ [the] Russia Collusion Hoax” [1]. In a matter of government spending, The Hill reports that the final cost for the Army's recent military parade held in Washington D.C. was $30 million [2]. Finally, the White House has made an uncorroborated claim, reported by Latin Times, that Hillary Clinton was on "'Daily Tranquilizers' for Mood Swings" during her time as Secretary of State; this claim has not appeared in other news sources in this feed and its veracity is unconfirmed [3].

### **Area 3: Congressional Activity and Politics**

**Topic 3.1: Legislative Proposals and Bipartisan Efforts**

A notable instance of bipartisan cooperation is taking shape in the Senate. Several Republican senators have joined their Democratic colleagues to introduce a bill aimed at exempting small businesses from President Trump's recently imposed tariffs on Canadian goods [1]. In the House, a new bill, H.R.4620, has been introduced that would amend federal law to "include rioting in the definition of racketeering activity" [2]. This legislative move to expand the scope of RICO laws aligns with recent public statements from Senator Ted Cruz, who has explicitly expressed a desire to apply such laws to individuals and groups alleged to be funding protests [3].

**References:**
[1] Republican senators join Dems on bill to exempt small businesses from Trump's Canada tariffs, https://www.cnbc.com/2025/07/23/trump-canada-tariffs-small-business-bill.html

[2] H.R.4620 - To amend title 18, United States Code, to include rioting in the definition of racketeering activity., https://www.congress.gov/bill/119th-congress/house-bill/4620?q=%7B%22search%22%3A%22congressId%3A119+AND+billStatus%3A%5C%22Introduced%5C%22%22%7D&s=1&r=4

[3] Ted Cruz wants to use RICO laws on alleged protest funders, https://www.chron.com/politics/article/ted-cruz-ice-palestine-protests-20782531.php

**Topic 3.2: Partisan Disputes, Censure, and Redistricting**

Partisan tensions are escalating over political boundaries and past controversies. Senator Elissa Slotkin (D-MI) has taken a hardline stance on redistricting, stating to Axios that she is prepared to go "'nuclear'" in response to GOP-led efforts in Texas [1]. In the House, a subcommittee voted to issue subpoenas to former President Bill Clinton and former Secretary of State Hillary Clinton; the subject of the inquiry is not specified in the headline [2]. Additionally, House Republicans are moving to formally censure a Democratic Representative named McIver. The Associated Press reports this action is related to an incident at a New Jersey detention center, but the headlines do not provide details about the specific nature of the incident [3].

**References:**
[1] Sen. Slotkin prepared to go "nuclear" over Texas redistricting, https://www.axios.com/2025/07/23/texas-redistricting-democrats-nuclear-slotkin

[2] House subcommittee votes in favor of subpoenaing Bill and Hillary Clinton, https://wjactv.com/news/nation-world/house-subcommittee-votes-in-favor-of-subpoenaing-bill-and-hillary-clinton-james-comey-jeffrey-epstein-ghislaine-maxwell-deposition-president-donald-trump

[3] House GOP seeks to censure Democrat McIver over New Jersey detention center incident, https://apnews.com/article/monica-mciver-ice-protest-censure-detention-centers-a221380e7b5dcebb32622eba267db222

### **Area 4: 2026 Elections and Campaigning**

**Topic 4.1: North Carolina Senate Race**

The 2026 electoral map is beginning to form, with a major development in North Carolina. According to Politico, former two-term Governor Roy Cooper, a Democrat, is planning to formally announce his entry into the U.S. Senate race on Monday [1]. NBC News reports that Democrats view Cooper as a "top recruit," highlighting his proven electoral success in having won six prior statewide elections for attorney general and governor. His candidacy is seen as a prime opportunity to flip a Republican-held seat in the key battleground state [2].

However, a subsequent report from the same outlet, citing an unnamed official, clarified that the White House is not denying that the President’s name appears in the files, creating public and political confusion [7]. This narrative is amplified by the separate emergence of photographs showing Jeffrey Epstein attending President Trump's 1993 wedding at Mar-a-Lago [8].

## 1. The Epstein Investigation

### 1.1 President Trump's Alleged Connection to Files

The controversy surrounding the Jeffrey Epstein files has intensified significantly, with multiple high-credibility reports alleging the President’s personal involvement. The New York Times reported that Attorney General Pam Bondi personally informed President Trump that his name appeared in the Epstein files [1, 2]. This briefing, which reportedly took place in the spring, also included the information that many other individuals were named in the files [3]. Crucially, this conversation reportedly occurred before the Department of Justice made the decision to withhold the documents from public release, a timeline underscored by stories from both CNBC and People magazine based on the Wall Street Journal's initial reporting [4, 5].

The White House’s public response has been inconsistent. It initially issued a statement to Reuters calling the Wall Street Journal's story "fake" [6]. However, a subsequent report from the same outlet, citing an unnamed official, clarified that the White House is not denying that the President’s name appears in the files, creating public and political confusion [7]. This narrative is amplified by the separate emergence of photographs showing Jeffrey Epstein attending President Trump's 1993 wedding at Mar-a-Lago [8].
